    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4863fcf2-0acf-49b4-83bf-40dc1433b74f'

  <span id="freeText11530228089710108548" style="display:none">THE DEPARTED HAVE ARRIVED.<br /> <br />The world is not the way it was. The dead have risen, and the living are under attack. The powerful Church of Real Truth, in charge since the government fell, has sworn to reimburse citizens being harassed by the deceased. Enter Chess Putnam, a fully tattooed witch and freewheeling ghost hunter. She’s got a real talent for banishing the wicked dead. But Chess is keeping a dark secret: She owes a lot of money to a murderous drug lord named Bump, who wants immediate payback in the form of a dangerous job that involves black magic, human sacrifice, a nefarious demonic creature, and enough wicked energy to wipe out a city of souls. Toss in lust for a rival gang leader and a dangerous attraction to Bump’s ruthless enforcer, and Chess begins to wonder if the rush is really worth it. Hell, yeah.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Does a "lust quadrangle" count? Love is too dangerous for Chess. It means looking at feelings she spends the entire book running from, with help from <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Does a "lust quadrangle" count? Love is too dangerous for Chess. It means looking at feelings she spends the entire book running from, with help from a wide array of drugs, sex, danger, and bad choices. <br /><br />Still, romance is a major theme. And I don't mean that as a euphemism for "porn." I mean relationship building, destroying, and questioning that intensifies in the second book. Like Kate Daniels, it's not that clear who "the one" is until at least the second book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285600472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer102502328952095130"><b>Updated 1/7/2015</b><br/><br/>Love how Chess/Terrible relationship is written. I might bump up this series into my faves. It surely stands the test of time. <br/><br/>As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/adult-review-unholy-ghosts-by-stacia-kane.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/>How do <i>you</i> decide which urban fantasy series you should read?<br/><br/>Let's be honest, there is like million and a half books in this genre, all with the same basic premise, assemblage of characters, mythology structure and story arcs. I, personally, do not even bother to read synopses of UF books any more, because, well, they are all th</span>
  <span id="freeText102502328952095130" style="display:none"><b>Updated 1/7/2015</b><br /><br />Love how Chess/Terrible relationship is written. I might bump up this series into my faves. It surely stands the test of time. <br /><br />As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/03/adult-review-unholy-ghosts-by-stacia-kane.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br />How do <i>you</i> decide which urban fantasy series you should read?<br /><br />Let's be honest, there is like million and a half books in this genre, all with the same basic premise, assemblage of characters, mythology structure and story arcs. I, personally, do not even bother to read synopses of UF books any more, because, well, they are all the same anyway. Only some trusty reader-friend's recommendation will do the trick. And, apparently, mentioning some hottie can be enough to perk up my interest. In the case of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>, <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/1/post/2012/02/adult-review-sacrificial-magic-by-stacia-kane.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Catie talked so poetically about this one Terrible</a>, that I just had to check him out. ASAP, naturally.<br /><br />So, Terrible. I am not terribly into Terrible yet, but, boy, do I see promise. You see, I do like when an author writes a man who is not particularly attractive, and then manages to make him sexy. If I strain my brain, I can think of only one guy in UF who is no Adonis, but whose personality and actions make him the hottest guy on the block. I kinda enjoy to be surprised and wooed like that. (Sadly, this other guy is a teenager, Derek in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7581.Kelley_Armstrong" title="Kelley Armstrong" rel="nofollow noopener">Kelley Armstrong</a>'s Darkest Powers trilogy). Like Catie said in her review, Terrible is not handsome, at least not in a traditional way and not to the main character at first, the dialect he talks in makes him sound a tad... dumb, and yet, and yet, Stacia Kane manages to slowly make him VERY appealing, by writing things like this:<br /><br /><i>A couple made out against the gritty stucco wall on the side of the club. Chess watched them for a second, embarrassed to do so but unable to turn away, something quiet and small twisting in her chest.<br /><br />The girl was a little thing, platinum blond, in a miniskirt and a pair of platform heels that looked like they weighed more than her entire body. Her thin legs crossed at the ankle behind the guy’s waist, while her tiny, pale hands dug into his back. Chess couldn’t see her face; it was almost entirely hidden by the guy’s hands, cupping her cheeks like he thought the bones might break. Chess didn’t think she’d ever been touched like that. A pang of pure envy ran through her.<br /><br />The girl caressed the back of his neck and lifted her hands to twine her fingers in his hair. His hips pressed forward, pinning her against the wall, and he dipped his head to kiss her throat. The light caught the prominent ridge of his brow and the crooked bump of his nose.<br /><br />It was Terrible.<br /><br />Heat rushed to her face. Yes, definitely Terrible. No wonder he’d blushed when she teased him about his sideburns. She’d never even thought of him as actually being interested in women. He seemed totally asexual to her, like instead of fucking he preferred beating people up. A silly assumption. He was a man, after all.</i><br /><br />I know exactly what you are doing here, Ms. Kane, and it's working.<br /><br />What did not work as well for me is Chess' characterization. Would it be too awful to say that I didn't feel like she was junky enough? Hear me out. Chess, the ghost banisher, is an addict, she takes pills, she snorts speed, always waiting for her next fix, etc, etc. But, reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a>, I never felt that this addiction was a vital part of her, her driving force, rather, it was something that she did, that she could easily put away, something that did not affect her work or her mental abilities much. I did not feel like I was in a head of a serious addict. Maybe my impression has something to do with the fact that the book is written in 3rd person and therefore there is a bit of a distance between the reader and the narrator. Or maybe reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/527869.Trainspotting_" title="Trainspotting  by Irvine Welsh" rel="nofollow noopener">Trainspotting</a> left me with a skewed view of what severe addiction is like for an addict. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/527869.Trainspotting_" title="Trainspotting  by Irvine Welsh" rel="nofollow noopener">Trainspotting</a>, I felt, put me at the center of an addict's mind, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a> did not.<br /><br />I will not be wasting time on summarizing the details of this story or its mythology. This post-ghostapocalyptic setting worked for me, so did the mystery and the characters. Whatever I say I liked about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a> will not work for everyone, like it happens with most genre fiction. I also think that the two main points of contention in this series will be the main character's addiction and the local dialect.<br /><br />The book was a good fit for me though. I look forward to reading more about Chess and Terrible. Terrible has more of his 6 ft 4 in (<i>everything</i> in proportion) glory and prowess to demonstrate. I am along for that ride.</span>
  <a data-text-id="102502328952095130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_117510460" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/117510460" />
    <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy"><img alt="Kat Kennedy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537750381p2/3270188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/117510460?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat Kennedy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat Kennedy" href="/user/show/3270188-kat-kennedy">Kat Kennedy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=the-great-shelf-of-meh">the-great-shelf-of-meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer117510460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2803734460921423223">If you've ever been one of those people lucky enough to be gifted without any specific fondness for chocolate or ice cream or sweets then you'll know what it's like to have someone look at you, horrified, and exclaim, "How? Chocolate/ice cream/lollies are so good!"<br/><br/>I would like to start off by saying that I'm prefectly aware that they're apparently very good. I don't mind lollies - as long as they're gummy bears I'll even eat them! I'll have chocolate occassionally but I generally avoid ice cream</span>
  <span id="freeText2803734460921423223" style="display:none">If you've ever been one of those people lucky enough to be gifted without any specific fondness for chocolate or ice cream or sweets then you'll know what it's like to have someone look at you, horrified, and exclaim, "How? Chocolate/ice cream/lollies are so good!"<br><br>I would like to start off by saying that I'm prefectly aware that they're apparently very good. I don't mind lollies - as long as they're gummy bears I'll even eat them! I'll have chocolate occassionally but I generally avoid ice cream. So you see, it's not that I've been stuck in a jungle in Borneo for the last 24 years and am simply ignorant of how good they are. I know. Family, friends, acquaintances, strangers, sales-people, the media and the world in general has been telling me how good they are for my entire life. <br><br>It's just not my bag, baby!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>My disinterest neither adds to their goodness nor subtracts from it. I promise. Except for Gummy Bears - they are the single most awesome force on the face of the planet. Just admit it already.<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br>The Gummy Bear Army will take care of you if you disagree!<br><br>So the thing about Unholy Ghosts wasn't that it wasn't pretty good. In fact, there are quite a few things that I will now praise the author for.<br><br>Terrible - one of the best male romantic characters created. Fantastic. The fact that she can make him so sexy yet ultimately describe him as ugly kind of does it for me.<br><br>The language - I loved the broken down English used in this story. it added a very realistic touch!<br><br>The Dystopian world - Creativity and the ability to see a different world are two things that I really enjoy about reading stories. It was intersting to read a story about a world built around maintaining the ghost threat.<br><br>The plot - well paced and interesting. I didn't catch myself getting bored at all.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380338582i/695603.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Okay, not MUCH! I only had eight rebel gummy bears tortured while reading this book.<br><br>But still there were some set backs.<br><br>The writing was sometimes choppy, sloppy and stroppy. Sentences sometimes were awkwardly jarred together like this!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The character of Chess kind of annoyed me too. Perhaps because... well... how do I put this delicately?<br><br>Okay. Well, my mummy says that everyone is born with different gifts. Some with kindness, others with empathy and others with a drive to succeed. And some people are gifted with the ability to be judgemental little bitches who get annoyed when people make stupid decisions.<br><br>I'll give you a moment to guess which one I have. Okay, I don't really care about drugs. They aren't my deal. I'd take gummy bears over speed any day, but it was more the cliched part of her character that annoyed me.<br><br>Foster child, abused and spent her life going from home to home. We've seen it over and over again in UF dames except Elena from Women of the Otherwold does it soooooooooooo much better. <br><br>The mystery is okay. Not fantabulous but not too, too easy to solve and the spooky atmosphere of the book definitely made it a better read for me as I went along.<br><br>So I won't put Chess up there with Elena, Cat, Kate, Merit or Mercy but it's not like this series is particularly bad either and if you're looking for a nice change from the devestatingly adonis-like men of the UF/PNR world then give this book a try.<br><br>If not, you're always welcome to join me with my gummy bears.<br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2803734460921423223" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer10423879609066289894">· A <b>MacHalo Freaks</b> buddy read! Yay and stuff! ·<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>DNF at 60%</b><br/><br/><b>I'm in a pretty foul mood these days</b> so I'm afraid this is not going to go well. Actually I don't even feel like reviewing this, I've wasted enough time with this book as it is. <b>BUT</b> I need to get it all out of my system <b>so here goes.</b><br/><br/><b>If you love this book</b> you might want to either take a few steps back or not read this review at all. If you do read it, don't even think of giving me hell about it afterwards, <b>I've had it with trolls.</b><br/><br/><b>What this </b></span>
  <span id="freeText10423879609066289894" style="display:none">· A <b>MacHalo Freaks</b> buddy read! Yay and stuff! ·<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423050384ra/13581493.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>DNF at 60%</b><br><br><b>I'm in a pretty foul mood these days</b> so I'm afraid this is not going to go well. Actually I don't even feel like reviewing this, I've wasted enough time with this book as it is. <b>BUT</b> I need to get it all out of my system <b>so here goes.</b><br><br><b>If you love this book</b> you might want to either take a few steps back or not read this review at all. If you do read it, don't even think of giving me hell about it afterwards, <b>I've had it with trolls.</b><br><br><b>What this book isn't:</b><br>✔ Original<br>✔ Weird<br>✔ Dark<br>✔ Creepy<br>✔ Gritty<br>✔ Horrific<br>✔ Gripping<br><br><b>I'm pretty sure</b> the author wanted the book to be all these things but guess what? <b>EPIC FAIL</b>.<br><br><b>What this book is:</b><br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br>✔ Boring<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423052284ra/13581667.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think the story had <b>potential</b>.<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think the world building was mind-blowingly <b>creative</b>.<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think the book was uber cool because drug use is a character in itself (<b>someone please kill me</b>).<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think the characters were either interesting or <b>well-developed</b>.<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think Chess was a badass (you're kidding right? <b>Please tell me you're kidding</b>).<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't like Terrible the "bad boy with a heart" (<b>can I scream here?</b>).<br>✘ <b>No</b> I didn't think the supposed "action" scenes were either exciting or <b>well-written</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423055314i/13582154.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that the author was trying too hard to be original and <b>failed miserably.</b><br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that this was one of the flattest, most unemotional, <b>lacklustre stories</b> I've ever read.<br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that the characters had zero depth and <b>less personality than barnacles.</b><br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that Chess was the weakest, <b>most pathetic heroine ever.</b><br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that Terrible was the <b>most clichéd character ever.</b> Then again I've probably seen too many noir movies from the 1940s.<br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that Terrible was the <b>lamest character name ever.</b><br>✔ <b>Yes</b> I thought that <b>I</b> would eventually OD from all <b>the drugs Chess was doing.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423055392i/13582159.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Anything else? Let me think.</b> Oh yes, I know. Please don't even think of selling me a UF series by telling me there will eventually be romance or a love story of sorts between some of the characters. This is <b>not what I'm looking for</b> when I read UF. If I want to read a freaking love story I'll get myself some PNR. <b>Get it? Good.</b><br><br><b>One last piece of advice for Chess:</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423054219i/13581985.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Are you still here?</b> I have to say writing this was one of the most cathartic experiences ever and I feel much better now. <b>Thanks for staying with me through it all.</b><br><br><b>Now time for me to go and read an actual book.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423053039ra/13581798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1075673994">
  <td colspan="2">

Nicotine, drugs, ghosts and a freakin’ love triangle. Hip hip hurrah! <br><br>This book was very difficult for me to read because of my lack of interest in all of these things. It’s just weird. I actually like weird things, there’s nothing more entertaining than watching a bunch of crazy people wearing their underwear over their heads and acting like The Avengers. <i>Downside Ghosts</i> is weird in an omg wtf kind of way. But people like it so good for them. Me? Meh. Not my kind of series.<br><br>Yes that means that I won’t give it a second chance.<br><br>No, I won’t change my mind.<br><br>Yes, it does suck that much.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1194071668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5352216397925593517"><b>4.5 Totally Surprised Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423606043i/13649743.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>BR with my awesome <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>MacHalo girls.</a><br/><br/><u>10 things I hate about Unholy Ghosts...</u></b><br/><br/>1) <b>Lex.</b> I don't like this guy. There is something really off about him. I don't trust him at all.<br/>2) <b>The drugs.</b> Huge pet-pieve of mine. I think that doing drugs shows weakness which the heroine proved right since everyone was using her drug addiction to push her around.<br/>3) <b>The Church.</b> They are fanatical and tyrannical.<br/>4) <b>The slang.</b> Too much... Too freakin much.<br/>5) <b>The love triangle.</b> No need for elabor</span>
  <span id="freeText5352216397925593517" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Totally Surprised Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423606043i/13649743.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>BR with my awesome <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo girls.</a><br><br><u>10 things I hate about Unholy Ghosts...</u></b><br><br>1) <b>Lex.</b> I don't like this guy. There is something really off about him. I don't trust him at all.<br>2) <b>The drugs.</b> Huge pet-pieve of mine. I think that doing drugs shows weakness which the heroine proved right since everyone was using her drug addiction to push her around.<br>3) <b>The Church.</b> They are fanatical and tyrannical.<br>4) <b>The slang.</b> Too much... Too freakin much.<br>5) <b>The love triangle.</b> No need for elaboration there. I hate love triangles and why that idiot(Chess) would ever choose Lex over Terrible is beyond me.<br>6) <b>Chess.</b> Because she is pathetic. I can't believe she actually crawled at Lexe's feet to get the pill.<br>7) <b>Chess.</b> Because she is a whiny mess whose only constant thought is her next high.<br>8) <b>Chess.</b> Because she was a coward. All she did was whine about how scared she was and get high to get through her day.<br>9) <b>Chess.</b> Because she was jumping to conclusions without any evidence and made a huge fuss based on nothing.<br>10) <b>Chess.</b> Because she was mean and hurt Terrible and she was too blind to even notice. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I will never forgive her having sex with Lex minutes after she'd crushed Terrible. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423606043i/13649744.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Things I loved about the book...</u>
</b><br><br>1) <b>Terrible.</b> I loved Terrible. He was like a vicious puppy, all snarly and bity but only because it had been hurt and kicked one too many times. I wanted to hug him and tell him everything would be all right.<br>2) <b>The plot line.</b> The plotline wasn't bad at all. I liked the twists and turns and I kept on guessing who the bad guy would be.(My bets were on lex but that didn't work out...)<br>3) <b>?</b><br>4) <b>?</b><br>5) <b>?</b><br>6) <b>?</b><br>7) <b>?</b><br>8) <b>?</b><br>9) <b>?</b><br>10) <b>?</b> I really have no idea why I liked this book so much. It pressed soooo many of my negative buttons that I should have DNFed it, but I just couldn't put it down. Despite the fact that I like none of the characters, except Terrible, despite the fact that I found the heroine as annoying as they come, despite my annoyance with the slang and the drugs, I freakin' loved this book. Maybe Stacia Kane has done magic to it??<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401416951ra/9800160.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_295028118" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/295028118" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/295028118?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007352814" href="/book/show/8086283-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Emily May by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295028118" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3217494723961935406"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I don't seem capable of finding a healthy medium when it comes to urban fantasy books - they either do nothing for me, or I develop a slight addiction. I can feel my love for this series forming already, this book was just so gory, nasty, fun and very very readable. It's been a long while since I've finished a book in just one day but I've been unable to put <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_' title='Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unholy Ghosts</a> down.<br/><br/>Once more, I owe thanks to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2250020' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tatiana</a> for bringing this book to my attention, I've been struggling with the urban fanta</span>
  <span id="freeText3217494723961935406" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don't seem capable of finding a healthy medium when it comes to urban fantasy books - they either do nothing for me, or I develop a slight addiction. I can feel my love for this series forming already, this book was just so gory, nasty, fun and very very readable. It's been a long while since I've finished a book in just one day but I've been unable to put <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6261189.Unholy_Ghosts__Downside_Ghosts___1_" title="Unholy Ghosts (Downside Ghosts, #1) by Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Unholy Ghosts</a> down.<br><br>Once more, I owe thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2250020" rel="nofollow noopener">Tatiana</a> for bringing this book to my attention, I've been struggling with the urban fantasy genre for a while now and, despite reading countless books about all kinds of supernatural creatures and mysteries, I've come away feeling disappointed and bored. I can't pinpoint exactly what it was that I loved about this book and that made it stand out from all the same old blandness I've come to expect, but I can tell you a few points that I'm sure contributed to winning me over, and hopefully this will help others decide whether the Downside Ghosts series is right for them.<br><br>Firstly, I liked that Chess was a faulty human being with problems - like a drug addiction - and regular fears. It's so hard to find that perfect balance: creating the kickass heroine we all want, but still allowing her to be human enough to relate to. I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1045593.Stacia_Kane" title="Stacia Kane" rel="nofollow noopener">Stacia Kane</a> did it superbly. Chess is not yet a favourite heroine of mine but I have faith in the character and am anxious to hear more about her paranormal escapades.<br><br>And Terrible. I saw immediately why he would not appeal to everyone... his disjointed speech and his less than pretty appearance. And yet I think this is exactly why I loved him. I've read so many novels, so so many where the possible love interest is supposedly all kinds of hot - perfect body, perfect facial features, great hair, dazzling smile... just a red hot pile of shiny perfection. But perfection is just so... dull. I want me an interesting, complicated guy who holds my attention at the times he's wearing clothes, as well as the times he isn't. Plus, no Chess/Terrible sexy times in this book, but this is a positive because sexual tension really makes me want to read on. Hehe.<br><br>I am very excited about this series. If I were to say anything negative, I would just like Chess to get herself a decent girlfriend to balance out the testosterone overload in the novel. Other than that, a great start to a series that I hear continues to get better.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3217494723961935406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer771462471" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13419435286399443089">★★★ for story + ★ for a guy named Terrible = ★★★★ stars<br/><br/>I'd heard about this series before, but just now finally got around to starting it with my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>MacHalo girls</a> in a buddy read.<br/><br/>Chess is a witch.<br/><br/>Not a witch like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198791i/13597014._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A little more like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198791i/13597015._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But she's more or less a good witch who works for the Church. It's present day, but in an alternate reality where ghosts got really pissed one day and decided to try and take over the planet, killing as many humans as they could. The Church got things under con</span>
  <span id="freeText13419435286399443089" style="display:none">★★★ for story + ★ for a guy named Terrible = ★★★★ stars<br><br>I'd heard about this series before, but just now finally got around to starting it with my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo girls</a> in a buddy read.<br><br>Chess is a witch.<br><br>Not a witch like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198791i/13597014._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A little more like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198791i/13597015._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But she's more or less a good witch who works for the Church. It's present day, but in an alternate reality where ghosts got really pissed one day and decided to try and take over the planet, killing as many humans as they could. The Church got things under control... and eradicated religion in the process. There's no God in this Church. <br><br>So Chess tries to find rogue ghosts and uses magic to send them back where they belong. She lives in a rough part of town, by choice. Probably mainly because it's easier to get the drugs she likes to take. So, she might not be on her toes all the time, but she gets the job done. <br><br>I liked Chess. She's not your typical heroine. She's always popping pills (she even <i>chews</i> them, none of this swallowing nonsense). Her idea of a relationship is a one-night stand. She's got issues. But it works for me. <br><br>But, what really worked for me, was TERRIBLE. He's not your average romantic type. He has scars, tattoos, a big nose... he's actually supposed to be a little ugly. But he's 6'4" with big hands, evenly proportioned all over (wink wink), he opens car doors for ladies, wears bowling shirts, is protective of children, kisses like a mo-fo, and dang, he's just sexy.<br><br>(I just found out about these people today, but James Quaintance and Pippa Holland - I guess they are models - are what I picture as Chess and Terrible.)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198255i/13596960._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198255i/13596961.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423198255i/13596962.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I think this books suffers from a few issues... it's the first in a series, some kinks are getting worked out, the pacing is slow at times, it's too early to get a real feel for the world and characters at times. But I will definitely be continuing with this. I can't wait to find out what happens next! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13419435286399443089" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_713406324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713406324" />
    <a title="Erica Ravenclaw" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12099580-erica-ravenclaw"><img alt="Erica Ravenclaw" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598276462p2/12099580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713406324?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erica Ravenclaw" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erica Ravenclaw" href="/user/show/12099580-erica-ravenclaw">Erica Ravenclaw</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007352814" href="/book/show/8086283-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Erica Ravenclaw by: </span>
      JennyJen
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12099580-erica-ravenclaw?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713406324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4699957746881817247">☆☆☆☆☆<br/><br/><b>Feb 2015 Reread with MacHalo Girls: ABSOLUTELY FUCKING LOVED IT. Everything I said below still stands. I think I loved it more the second time around because <i>perspective.</i></b><br/><br/><b> No Spoilers! Definitely colorful language abound! </b><br/><br/><br/><b>1. THIS IS NOT WHAT I WAS EXPECTING.</b><br/><br/>I didn't read the reviews on this until I finished, and truthfully it's really a difficult book to review. It's not what you think it's going to be. It's not what you want it to be. It's not familiar. It's not unfamiliar. So what is it th</span>
  <span id="freeText4699957746881817247" style="display:none">☆☆☆☆☆<br><br><b>Feb 2015 Reread with MacHalo Girls: ABSOLUTELY FUCKING LOVED IT. Everything I said below still stands. I think I loved it more the second time around because <i>perspective.</i></b><br><br><b> No Spoilers! Definitely colorful language abound! </b><br><br><br><b>1. THIS IS NOT WHAT I WAS EXPECTING.</b><br><br>I didn't read the reviews on this until I finished, and truthfully it's really a difficult book to review. It's not what you think it's going to be. It's not what you want it to be. It's not familiar. It's not unfamiliar. So what is it then? It's fucking tragic. This world is a place with no meaning. Filled with a bunch of people with no hope. The class devision is extremely prevalent, specifically noted in the dialect of the lower class. It's a bit startling at first, but truthfully it's something you adjust to and eventually see the fineness the author applied to it. It speaks of an uneducated and hardened group of people who have long been forgotten by a system that no longer seems to exist. There is no god, no light, no better place, no peace. You simply die, and your ghost is ushered to the underground where once a year you might be let out, for all of eternity, consumed by a murderous rage, you aren't even yourself. Let that sink in for a moment, shall we? You get this brief time of being alive where the quality of your life is nothing more than a roll of the dice. You are born with magic? Great. You are born with wealthy parents? Good. You are born poor? Well, shit. You can't change anything, you just have to manage to make it through, then for what exactly? AN ETERNITY OF NOTHING BUT RAGE IN THE CITY UNDERGROUND!<br><br><b>2. WHO ARE THESE CHARACTERS? IS THAT A LOVE TRIANGLE? I DON'T EVEN CARE. </b><br><br>You see, anything to do with ghosts typically freaks me the feck out and so that means I'm in equal measure terrified and fascinated. Eventually my TBR list lacked the ability to hold my attention and I went out seeking something I couldn't articulate. Thankfully I've met some book soul sisters here on GR and was reminded yet again by Jenny of this series. Something sparked and I put all my other reads on hold to start this.<br>I made a note at 20% through to myself: <br><b> Even if I were to stop right now, even if that was possible to let these characters go, I would always remember Chess. She is a character that will stay with me forever. </b><br><br>She is mosaic of painful memories, self-medicating tendencies and a healthy dose of self loathing. She is powerful, deeply sensitive, and brimming with hope despite herself. She <i> expects </i> the worst in others but somehow finds herself disappointed when they let her down. She is acutely aware of herself yet slathered in denial. She is a junkie with morals. She is a powerful witch and debunker but afraid of ghosts. She is gritty, raw and articulate. She is a badass and a pussy. She is complex, she is herself, she is MY NEW FAVORITE CHARACTER. <br><br><a href="http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/anigif_original-grid-image-11454-1410879583-6_zps120e1470.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1416703120ra/12045730.gif" alt=" photo anigif_original-grid-image-11454-1410879583-6_zps120e1470.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Terrible is equally complex and manages to ooze a comfort in his own skin typically only seen in those who have been blessed with the pleasure of growing old. As all of the characters in this series his many layers are revealed in a deliciously slow manner, and almost in spite of himself. Terrible doesn't want you to get to know him but every now and again he slips and you see how clever, observant and protective he is. Not only does Terrible accept himself without hesitation despite being who he is and what he does, he also offers the same acceptance to all those around him. He truly see's people for who they are without any preconceived idea's of what they should do or be or say. This is especially visible in the way his friendship with Chess builds over the series. <br><br>Lex is the obvious charmer but carries it as his armor. You never once assume he will be anything other than what he is. I accept him, he's interesting and offers what I imagine will be a tough thing to accept in the plot. The relationship that develops with Chess is one she may have a very hard time seeing for what it really is.<br><br><i>Really, all of these characters are easy to judge and disconnect from. Some are junkies, some are pushers, some are enforcers and murderers, some abusive to themselves and to others. They will reflect all the ugly humanity has to offer and it's up to the reader to look deeper and see all aspects of their story. </i><br><br><b>3. THIS PLOT. WHAT IS HAPPENING. IS THIS HAPPENING?</b><br><br>N-O-T-H-I-N-G about this book is something you've read before. The drug use is intense and is a character of it's own. It's the force that drives everything Chess does, from sleeping, to working, to relaxing, to functioning on a basic level. It has a sort of love triangle but so far from the YA garbage you've read that you won't even care. These ghosts are murderous and dangerous. This world is bizarre and confusing. THIS FUCKING PLOT IS AMAZEBALLS AND CREEPS UP ON YOU.<br><br><a href="http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/anigif_enhanced-buzz-6863-1387487310-6_zps02958714.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388369682ra/7812509.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-6863-1387487310-6_zps02958714.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>4. EVERYTHING ABOUT THIS BOOK. </b><br><br><a href="http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/OVkHnge_zpsttgqviyq.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1419950062ra/13149904.gif" alt=" photo OVkHnge_zpsttgqviyq.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br><br><b>5. THE 2ND BOOK IS ON MY KINDLE. I HAVE TO FUCKING GO.</b><br><br><a href="http://s1212.photobucket.com/user/PetiteAme/media/Halloween%20Upload/GIFS/anigif_enhanced-buzz-29335-1387400569-34_zps7b2663b9.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388369682ra/7812511.gif" alt=" photo anigif_enhanced-buzz-29335-1387400569-34_zps7b2663b9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://www.ericapetiteame.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1397955482i/9350858.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4699957746881817247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=urban-fantasy-uf">urban-fantasy-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=owned-kindle">owned-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3104032-regina?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111904586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2963925908852405298">4-4.5 stars. Oh My Goodness! This book blew me away. First, I have to say I really steer clear of movies and books that paint drug use as fun (not talking about pot/marijuana). For some reason it just really turns my stomach. I don't judge the users morally but I just can't watch the downward spiral, the descent. So I really was reluctant to pick up this book. But I am so glad that I did. The lead character Cesaria a/k/a "Chess" is a difficult person to focus on for over 300 pages. But Stacia Ka</span>
  <span id="freeText2963925908852405298" style="display:none">4-4.5 stars. Oh My Goodness! This book blew me away. First, I have to say I really steer clear of movies and books that paint drug use as fun (not talking about pot/marijuana). For some reason it just really turns my stomach. I don't judge the users morally but I just can't watch the downward spiral, the descent. So I really was reluctant to pick up this book. But I am so glad that I did. The lead character Cesaria a/k/a "Chess" is a difficult person to focus on for over 300 pages. But Stacia Kane makes the experience enthralling. I love dark urban fantasy and in this book an alternate reality is created, one where something happened in 1997 throughout the world, that forever changed the course of the world. That time is called, "BT" -- Before Truth. Christianity is gone, religious faith is gone. There is supposedly no belief in a higher power, only a belief in magic. The new "Church" controls the world and protects everyone from ghosts who seek to kill people. Kane makes references to bands, punk culture and for me it was very comforting, homey. She somehow creates this very different world, with a community that has an odd style of speaking english, but yet it is still familiar. There are no clear heroes or heroines in this book. But the reader definitely roots for Chess -- despite her repeated bad choices. <br /><br />The main male character, "Terrible", is someone who is helping her in this adventure, he is physically unappealing, a violent man -- but somehow Kane creates a deep three dimensional character out of this template and he is very sympathetic. <br /><br />There are some awkward and emotionally uncomfortable scenes between Chess and Terrible, Kane makes the reader feel them. I could feel Chess' embarrassment and I so felt bad for Terrible. Wonderful first book in a very dark urban fantasy. I cannot wait to read #2!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2963925908852405298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3197637165514769709" style="display:none">Unholy Ghosts<br />Downside Ghosts, Book 1<br />By: Stacia Kane<br />Narrated by: Bahni Turpin<br />This is an amazing book! <div id="review_107639971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107639971" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107639971?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-july-2011">zzread-july-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=first-in-series">first-in-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=wizards">wizards</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107639971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5510617541552979980"><br/><br/>I never expected to like this book.<br/><br/>I had read all sorts of reviews and most of them were fairly positive but to read a story about a heroine with a drug addiction problem (no pun intended) – I wasn’t sure if this book would be for me.<br/><br/><i>Unholy Ghosts</i> is a dark, dirty, gritty, read. The world building is imaginative. Set in a world where ghosts need to be controlled by debunkers, drug lords roam freely, and magic exists, <i>Unholy Ghosts</i> is a compelling read.<br/><br/>The main character Chess (Cesaria) Putman is</span>
  <span id="freeText5510617541552979980" style="display:none"><br /><br />I never expected to like this book.<br /><br />I had read all sorts of reviews and most of them were fairly positive but to read a story about a heroine with a drug addiction problem (no pun intended) – I wasn’t sure if this book would be for me.<br /><br /><i>Unholy Ghosts</i> is a dark, dirty, gritty, read. The world building is imaginative. Set in a world where ghosts need to be controlled by debunkers, drug lords roam freely, and magic exists, <i>Unholy Ghosts</i> is a compelling read.<br /><br />The main character Chess (Cesaria) Putman is a debunker for the church. In this world, the church is akin to the government. Chess is a kind of a witch. She wears special magical tattoos and carries all sorts of magical paraphernalia. <br /><br />Chess is very good at her job. Chess is also a drug addict, high as a kite most of the time. I found that Chess’ obsession with drugs was a little disconcerting for me. Sure, she functions well, but how effective can she be when she owes the local drug lord a lot of money. Her addictions make her a pawn of anyone that can feed her addiction. She feels no remorse; she makes no attempt to reduce her usage or detoxify. Her view of the world through the drug induced haze is very egocentric.<br /><br />The drug usage acts as an entry ticket to the underworld of her city. She gains access to places that would not be open to her otherwise. <br /><br />I loved the characters in this book. They were well fleshed out, with a lot of depth. I loved Terrible – an enforcer with a sense of honor. <br /><br />The action scenes were spectacular. I sat at the edge of my seat and experienced the darkness, the fear, and the panic of the main character. The scene at the airport was absolutely breathtaking and scary at the same time.<br /><br />I can’t wait to read the next book in the series. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5510617541552979980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_438243494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/438243494" />
    <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time"><img alt="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365526640p2/13070326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/438243494?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather K (dentist in my spare time)" href="/user/show/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time">Heather K (dentist in my spare time)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/15836717-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=beta-heros-in-mf">beta-heros-in-mf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=price-was-right-2-99-or-less">price-was-right-2-99-or-less</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=addiction-or-mental-disorders">addiction-or-mental-disorders</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=ghosts-spirits">ghosts-spirits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=first-in-a-series-i-love">first-in-a-series-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13070326-heather-k-dentist-in-my-spare-time?shelf=narrator-very-good">narrator-very-good</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer438243494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9092658362323768379"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg' width='200' height='150' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>A good narrator can always make or break a book for me. In this case, I think my eventual affection for this story was due in a large part to Bahni Turpin, who managed to flawlessly execute both the male and female voices. She made these characters come alive, and I went from not feeling the book to really loving it. This book has some difficult speech patterns in it, and I think hearing a narrator read it aloud made it feel urban and authentic. <br/><br/>I tend to like my urban fantasy books to be just t</span>
  <span id="freeText9092658362323768379" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472750173i/20237706._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>A good narrator can always make or break a book for me. In this case, I think my eventual affection for this story was due in a large part to Bahni Turpin, who managed to flawlessly execute both the male and female voices. She made these characters come alive, and I went from not feeling the book to really loving it. This book has some difficult speech patterns in it, and I think hearing a narrator read it aloud made it feel urban and authentic. <br><br>I tend to like my urban fantasy books to be just that: Urban fantasy. I like the focus to be on the plot and the action with any romance playing a small role. This book delivered on that in spades. It was dark, scary at times, and with some real gritty action. I think the world-building was great. I totally grasped the concept of the Church of Truth and the role of the debunkers. Stacia Kane did a great job in that department. <br><br>My real issue with this book is with Chess, the main character. I found her to be extremely difficult to like. I never thought myself to be prudish about drugs, but I didn't like her junkie persona and her cavalier treatment of those around her. I had a hard time relating to her and it took until around the 60% mark for me to warm to Chess. <br><br>I loved all of the secondary characters, especially Terrible. It was a breath of fresh air to read about a possible love interest who is not conventionally attractive. He was <i>interesting</i> and unexpected. Also, Bahni Turpin managed to make his voice freaking sexy. <br><br>All in all, I'm determined to read this series through, but only in the audible version. I loved the listening experience and am excited to hear what happens next to my ambivalent junkie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9092658362323768379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2130091457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18135652213717061592">I was really looking forward to liking this book but I have a huge trigger (or two) and that is drug abuse. The heroine is what seems always getting high and is also indebted to her dealer who is also a pimp. I really disliked that, so I sadly had to drop the story. Also, what's with all the Church thing. It's like the whole world is enslaved by it and it's, at least to me, not a normal church but more of a sect that rulls the world. The whole plot thus just wasn't for me. If you can overlook al</span>
  <span id="freeText18135652213717061592" style="display:none">I was really looking forward to liking this book but I have a huge trigger (or two) and that is drug abuse. The heroine is what seems always getting high and is also indebted to her dealer who is also a pimp. I really disliked that, so I sadly had to drop the story. Also, what's with all the Church thing. It's like the whole world is enslaved by it and it's, at least to me, not a normal church but more of a sect that rulls the world. The whole plot thus just wasn't for me. If you can overlook all that, then go for it. Maybe you'll enjoy the story more than me. :)<br /></span>

<div id="review_120995852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/120995852" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/120995852?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">lovers of urban fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Penny by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/541201-wicked-incognito-now">Wicked Incognito Now</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=penny-s-favorite-books">penny-s-favorite-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=grrrl-power">grrrl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=witchy-woman">witchy-woman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer120995852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15729583368749084675">I'm going to start this review off on a tangent--when do I not? As far as I'm concerned 2011 has been the Year of Meh. Television has been practically unwatchable. Movies released this year: heinous. The books were, at best, mediocre. Admittedly, there were a few notable exceptions but, for the most part, I'm disappointed. <br/><br/>Over the past six months I've grown weary; struggled to finish most of what I've started, and, by the way, failing more often then not--you should see my pile of abandoned boo</span>
  <span id="freeText15729583368749084675" style="display:none">I'm going to start this review off on a tangent--when do I not? As far as I'm concerned 2011 has been the Year of Meh. Television has been practically unwatchable. Movies released this year: heinous. The books were, at best, mediocre. Admittedly, there were a few notable exceptions but, for the most part, I'm disappointed. <br /><br />Over the past six months I've grown weary; struggled to finish most of what I've started, and, by the way, failing more often then not--you should see my pile of abandoned books. Because of this I've been feeling the need to take a step back, maybe not read so much. Maybe spend my money more wisely--it is ridiculous how much I spend on books and audiobooks. You know, take a break. <br /><br />2011 killed my love of books (and movies and television). <br /><br />That said, over the past couple of days I've fallen in love with books (and reading) all over again. I'm in love. Love I tell ya. Can't-get-enough-make-everyone-sick-can't-eat-or-sleep-head-over-heels in love. Me and reading? It's like we're on a second honeymoon. I have Stacia Kane and her Downside Ghost series to thank because of it. <br /><br />I know, I know--none of the books in the Downside Ghost series were published this year. It doesn't matter. What does matter is I love reading. Again. <br /><br />Funny thing, it's not like Downside Ghosts is The Best Series, Ever. And it has to be said: it's definitely not for everyone. However, as far as I'm concerned, it is compelling and addictive. It's good. <br /><br />So. Unholy Ghosts. Where to start? Twenty-five year old Cesaria "Chess" Putnum is a hot mess, and not in that chick-flick cliche can't-get-my-life-together-because-I'm-so-adorably-clumsy-and-I-wear-glasses-that-make-me-look-unfortunate-until-I-finally-remove-them-during-the-makeover-montage-and-that's-when-everyone-discovers-I'm-super-hot sort of way. I mean the sort of hot mess that's boozy and pops pills all the live-long day.<br /><br />I'm not going to lie to you. I avoided this series for that exact reason. Boozy pill-poppers just aren't my thing, or so I thought. <br /><br />Then, other day, I was looking through my Kindle bookshelf and I noticed that I had the sample of Unholy Ghosts--for the life of me, I can't remember when I downloaded it. Curious, figuring I had nothing to lose, I decided to give it a chance before I went ahead and removed it. Imagine my surprise when I realized I couldn't go the rest of my life without reading more. So I purchased it (FYI, the Kindle edition of Unholy Ghosts is just 99 cents). <br /><br />The thing I like about Chess is, well, I pretty much like everything. Honestly, I don't even mind that she's a drug addict. Of course, most of her problems wouldn't happen if she wasn't addicted to pills, but if that were the case Unholy Ghosts wouldn't be so good. <br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of Chess's life her employment. She works for the Church of Real Truth as a Debunker, a person who goes around trying to debunk claims of hauntings. If she's able to then she gets a bonus and if she isn't, if the haunting is authentic, the homeowner is compensated by the church and the debunker will rid the home of the ghost. <br /><br />Sidenote: Did I mention this is a dystopian urban fantasy? Because it is. Basically way back in the year 1997 ghosts escaped wherever it is ghosts go (or actually The City, as it's called in this series) and got all murdery, killing one-third of the world's population. At the time The Church of Truth was just a small organization but they succeeded in capturing all the ghosts. 25 years later The Church of Truth is the only religion. They pretty much run the government too. Worldwide. <br /><br />The church has vowed to keep people safe from ghosts, which is why homeowners are compensated if their haunting is real. /sidenote<br /><br />Chess is good at being a Debunker and it's something she's proud of. She also loves the Church of Truth, despite the fact that it reigns supreme. I can't fault her for it because everything else in her life is crap--growing up being passed from abusive foster home to abusive foster home will mess you up, you know? And anyway the Church is the only place she's ever felt safe, the only thing that's ever given her life value. <br /><br />Anyway, things get really interesting when Chess's drug dealer blackmails her into working for him. &lt;--and I'm stopping right there because I don't want to ruin it for you. Plus, this review is entirely too long. <br /><br />This isn't my favorite book in the series, there are a few things that didn't exactly work for me, but I still like it. (Just so you know Unholy Magic, the second book in the Downside Ghost series is...um...<i>intense</i>. I'll be reviewing it soon). Three stars. <br /><br />P.S. This review is also posted at <a href="http://pennystuppence.blogspot.com/2011/12/review-unholy-ghosts-downside-ghosts-1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15729583368749084675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_334165696" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334165696" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476704-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333052331p2/7476704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334165696?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/7476704-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334165696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17957040760074704964">I’m going 4.5 and if I had to pay for stars it would probably be 4 but this book was just perfect timing for me and the ending put it over the top. The only thing stopping me from a straight 5 is that the character and world development really took a long time. <br/><br/>The writing was incredible to me. It is the kind of stuff I look for in a book. I'm not talking about the unique language either(I could have done with or without it) although the language really spoke to how true she was to the world she</span>
  <span id="freeText17957040760074704964" style="display:none">I’m going 4.5 and if I had to pay for stars it would probably be 4 but this book was just perfect timing for me and the ending put it over the top. The only thing stopping me from a straight 5 is that the character and world development really took a long time. <br /><br />The writing was incredible to me. It is the kind of stuff I look for in a book. I'm not talking about the unique language either(I could have done with or without it) although the language really spoke to how true she was to the world she built. Of course the people scraping by aren’t going to speak the language properly. There is nothing sugar coated in this book. The actions of the people are as dark as the world that was created for them. As dark and nasty as everything was it all felt like it belonged there. <br /><br />Chess is a seriously drug addicted Debunker (a kind of witch) for the Church who’s job it is to look into claims of people having ghosts. She gathers evidence to prove them wrong or she has to banish the ghosts back to the “City” if they turn out to be real. Of course her life would be much easier if she were just dealing with liars but her life becomes complicated when she has to deal with some serious Ghosts. If that weren’t enough her drug addiction has her juggling a lot of other balls in the air dealing with her drug dealers and has her paired with Terrible an unlikely ally who is her drug dealers/enforcer.<br /><br />Chess's sarcasm works so well with her character. Where many characters lately have been characters that have things going for them and they are all sarcastic. With Chess's character you can really<br />feel the anger and it really belongs in her character.<br /><br />“If Mrs. Morton would stop verbally jacking off her husband and son,this would all be done so much more quickly”<br /><br />It is exactly the kind of thing some struggling addict might say to herself when dealing with a rich snob in her suburban neighborhood.<br /><br />The descriptions of the rooms, and neighborhoods and even the people were so detailed it really drew a picture of where she was but not so much that it was rambling. I was so into her character I was pretty anxious most of the time while reading this book. When exploring Downside I felt strung out from Chess's lack of sleep, felt like I needed a shower after exploring tunnels and wanted to light a scented candle after exploring some of the places she went. It was meant to be dark and there is no warm and fuzzy going on here. <br /><br />Bottom line Chess is a complicated character. I don't even know what I feel for her. Terrible was awesome and I'm looking forward to these two interacting in the future. ( I hope. ) Throwing that 5th star at it was tough because the meat of the story doesn't really get good till almost 70% of the book. I knew towards the end it was going to be a 4.5 book and I didn't know which way I was going to go. I actually enjoyed the descriptive ride of Downside and the end of the book was the tipping point for me. To be so anxious through the whole book and then make me physically laugh at the end ( and I'm smiling while writing this) was so unexpected it still surprises me. At no point did I expect to walk away from this book with a smile on my face from laughing. (satisfied yeah laughing no)<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the scene at the end with Doyle when she tried to hide his name from Lex and he gets all indignant and says "my name is Doyle" and then Lex chases him to kick his ass and she doesn't even try and stop him...haha I loved it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I will definitely be moving on with the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17957040760074704964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
