  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_464544746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/464544746" />
    <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party"><img alt="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562621595p2/10923016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464544746?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party">David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=dastardly-villainesses">dastardly-villainesses</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=dashing-heroines">dashing-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464544746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8711094085324097272"><i>This book benefits from a compelling story, as well as a unique and fascinating mythology...it's just too bad that the </i><b>Unholy Ghosts</b><i> that haunt the city of Downside are far more interesting than the people who are trying to stop them!</i> <br/><br/>Chess Putnam is an ordained Debunker for the all-powerful Church of Real Truth. On a good day, she receives a generous bonus for proving someone is faking a haunting in order to extort money from the Church. On a bad day, the haunting turns out to be real, and Ches</span>
  <span id="freeText8711094085324097272" style="display:none"><i>This book benefits from a compelling story, as well as a unique and fascinating mythology...it's just too bad that the </i><b>Unholy Ghosts</b><i> that haunt the city of Downside are far more interesting than the people who are trying to stop them!</i> <br /><br />Chess Putnam is an ordained Debunker for the all-powerful Church of Real Truth. On a good day, she receives a generous bonus for proving someone is faking a haunting in order to extort money from the Church. On a bad day, the haunting turns out to be real, and Chess is charged with exorcising the ghost. Now Chess is facing her worst day ever. Her secret drug habit has gotten so out of control, she now owes $15,000 to a ruthless supplier. The only way out of her debt is to clean up a haunted airport for her dealer...which would land her in trouble with yet another dangerous drug lord. Add to that the supernatural entity that is stalking her at every turn...something more powerful than anything she has ever encountered. If Chess isn't careful, she just may wind up being the next ghost to haunt Downside...<br /><br />For me, the two most important elements of any book are the story and the characters, and the story within <i>Unholy Ghosts</i> deserves five stars easily! I absolutely loved the rich history of Downside and the Church of Real Truth. In this alternate history, everyone became disillusioned with all forms of government and religion after they were unable to prevent a ghostly invasion from wiping out one-third of the world's population. Only the Church of Real Truth was able to vanquish the evil ghosts, and as a result, the Church is now firmly in control. This is already an intriguing concept, and Stacia Kane capitalizes on it by throwing in so many extra details. I loved how every chapter started with a quote from the Church of Truth's various propaganda. I was fascinated by some of the more bizarre elements of the Church, like how the elders all dressed like modern-day pilgrims.<br /><br />In addition to an enthralling backstory, Chess Putnam's quest to learn who has been practicing forbidden black magic rituals is exciting as well. The story moves at a very fast pace, and while the book may be found on the fantasy shelves, Stacia Kane proves she can stand toe to toe with just about any horror writer as well. The supernatural elements in this book are nothing short of thrilling, where every type of ghost has their own nuances, and Kane expertly blends traditional ghost lore with her own unique ideas. I would love to go into more detail about some of the more original ideas that blew me away, but these things are better left to the imagination, and Kane's imagination is much more fun to experience firsthand!<br /><br />So...does it seem strange that I'm lavishing so much praise on a book when I only gave it three stars? Well, now we come to the other all-important element, and while Kane succeeds brilliantly in giving us a compelling story, she fails miserably in making the characters compelling as well. It's no exaggeration when I say I pretty much hated every single main character in the book! Granted, some characters were supposed to be annoying, like Chess's creepy drug-dealer Bump and her whiny fellow Debunker Doyle. But even the characters we were supposed to be rooting for are unpleasant to read about, especially Chess herself! In truth, I was intrigued when I first heard that the lead character was a drug addict, as it was a rather untraditional approach, but the biggest problem with Chess is that her vices are used as a substitute for any type of depth. She doesn't display much compassion, personality, or wit, just about anything Chess says or does comes back to drugs somehow! It's like the little kid who discovers the F-word for the first time and thinks all he has to do is keep saying it to make people laugh...when the author feels the need to reference Chess's drug habit on just about every page, it loses it's shock value and just becomes dull and repetitive after a while.<br /><br />There was another reason Chess didn't work for me, and that's because she doesn't really do a whole lot in the book. I like my urban-fantasy heroines to be strong, formidable and charismatic. Unfortunately, Chess often feels like a supporting player in her own book! She very rarely solves anything herself, instead her answer to everything is either to pop a pill or let some man (usually Bump's brutal enforcer Trouble) come to her rescue. Silly me, when I heard the book starred a ghost hunter with magical abilities, I just assumed she would be a force to be reckoned with, but Chess only has two moments in the entire book where she seems capable of handling something herself, and she manages to botch even one of those up! Honestly, Chess is such a cliched damsel-in-distress at times, I half-expected to see Snidely Whiplash tying her to train tracks at some point!<br /><br />So, <i>Unholy Ghosts</i> features a story worth reading, but no one worth reading about. Still, Stacia Kane did impress me with her brilliant imagination and her ability to write spine-tingling horror, so I would still be willing to give the Downside Ghosts series another chance. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8711094085324097272" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136832183" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136832183" />
    <a title="Felicia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666892-felicia"><img alt="Felicia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437521850p2/666892.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136832183?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Felicia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Felicia" href="/user/show/666892-felicia">Felicia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=urban-paranormal">urban-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/666892-felicia?shelf=vaginal-urban-fantasy">vaginal-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136832183" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4593935506430351236">GUYS...I dunno. I liked this book despite myself. It's super gritty, has an interesting worldbuilding, and I gave it 4 stars just for avoiding a lot of cliches I'm really tired of lately. But I gotta say, I am really on the fence about the lead character.<br/><br/>SPOILER:<br/>Basically she is a drug addict, and all the trouble in the book stems from that fact. I think it's REALLY cool and bold choice to have a character like this, (and have two kinda low-class, nebulously shaded love interests), and I enjoyed</span>
  <span id="freeText4593935506430351236" style="display:none">GUYS...I dunno. I liked this book despite myself. It's super gritty, has an interesting worldbuilding, and I gave it 4 stars just for avoiding a lot of cliches I'm really tired of lately. But I gotta say, I am really on the fence about the lead character.<br /><br />SPOILER:<br />Basically she is a drug addict, and all the trouble in the book stems from that fact. I think it's REALLY cool and bold choice to have a character like this, (and have two kinda low-class, nebulously shaded love interests), and I enjoyed this because it wasn't cliched like most. My problem is that if you have a character who's obviously making bad choices, like be a drug addict, then you'd want SOMEONE in her life to be like, "Hey, you shouldn't be a drug addict", and maybe have a few moments where the character is like, "Hmm, maybe I should stop this drug thing." I mean, that would be more tense, but basically she unrepentantly pops pills the whole book, and has no one in her life telling her it's not cool. Now, i THINK that the overall arc of the whole SERIES might be aiming to clean her up, but for a novel, I really felt like she needed some growth in this area, if this is the major conflict.<br /><br />THAT SAID, I really enjoyed this book. I also think guys would enjoy it as well, it's not so dominated by romance to make it strictly lady-appealing. I thought the Church and the world history was really fascinating too, so basically I'm reading the next book now, but it's hard to love this main character, NOT because of the drug addiction, but because of her repentance about it. We'll see where it goes! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4593935506430351236" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_478043471" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478043471" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580475762p2/12928663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478043471?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Brenna by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12928663-brenna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478043471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10517878198868337966"><b>4.5 stars. Great start to a series I know I am going to love!</b><br/><br/><i>Unholy Ghosts</i> had a little bit of everything that I love in a good book. The writing was great, the mood was dark and intriguing, the characters were flawed, lovable, and complex. There’s action, suspense, romance, some steam, and a fabulously built world. <br/><br/>It is told by Chess, our heroine, in third person POV. She is a Debunker for the Church. The Church isn’t religious in this world; it’s like their form of government that is ruled th</span>
  <span id="freeText10517878198868337966" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars. Great start to a series I know I am going to love!</b><br /><br /><i>Unholy Ghosts</i> had a little bit of everything that I love in a good book. The writing was great, the mood was dark and intriguing, the characters were flawed, lovable, and complex. There’s action, suspense, romance, some steam, and a fabulously built world. <br /><br />It is told by Chess, our heroine, in third person POV. She is a Debunker for the Church. The Church isn’t religious in this world; it’s like their form of government that is ruled through magic, Truth, and Fact. They took over after Haunted Week (which happened twenty something years prior)- the week when all ghosts surfaced and were actively attacking humans. So, Chess’s job as a Debunker is to investigate claims made by people about hauntings. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>Before Haunted Week—before the Church showed the world what Truth was—they’d been a tiny group, devoted to the theory and study of magic. Now they ran the world. And she was part of it. It was the one thing in her life of which she was proud.</blockquote>
</i><br />Chess is also a junkie. I knew this prior to starting this book and I have to say, it only made me want to read it more. Her addiction has put her in a tough spot. She owes her dealer, Bump A LOT of money. To settle her debt, he asks her to use her powers as a witch to do him a favor. This leads to her working closely with Bump’s right hand man, Terrible. As the story progresses, more characters enter the mix. Chess has to balance her job with the Church, paying Bump back, a rival gang member, Lex, offering her another out, and a potential conspiracy. <br /><br />This book is pretty dark and it’s done so well. It’s set in Downside, which is a very rundown area, pretty much just a ghetto. There’s poverty, drugs, prostitution, you name it. The descriptive writing really allows you to imagine exactly what this area is like and feel the underlying malevolence. The characters of this area also have a certain dialect. I think it’s called “Bump speak?” but I think it should be called “Down speak.” It’s really hard to explain, but it’s very slang based and pretty much every grammar rule in English is thrown out the window. Lots of ayes, nays, ain’ts, missing words, and my favorite, “dig?” While it took some getting used to, I found it fascinating and thought it only helped me to picture this world and get into the setting more. Chess does not speak this way though; it’s mostly the men – Bump, Terrible, Lex.<br /><br />What I loved most about this book was just the potential. I wasn’t immediately sucked in, but the latter half of the book really got my blood pumping. The whole book is actually quite intense because there is this dark, dangerous feel to everything. So many smaller things happen along the way then BOOM this huge LONG finale of sorts. And I think it has this HUGE potential to completely steal my heart and that’s because of Terrible.<br /><br />This guy is no average hero. He’s a bad guy. He’s supposedly ugly. He’s the most feared guy in downside, doing all Bump’s dirty work. Killing, beating, doing whatever is needed. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>Terrible was coming, his gait easy and steady, but the way his gaze fixed on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Doyle <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and the tire iron dangling loosely from his hand were more eloquent than anything else could have been.</blockquote>
</i><br />Then he starts working with Chess and has to help her with her favor for Bump. The whole way through he is always there for her and protecting her. There is so much more to him, he’s not this big oaf that he appears to be and I love that he is so damaged and different from the perfect, model like guys in a lot of books. The fact that he’s described as ugly at times, and I still find myself falling for him and thinking he’s sexy is a testament to how awesome this guy is. The romance is very understated, it’s sexual tension at its finest. There are multiple “love interests” I guess you would call them, but they are all interesting in their own ways – good/bad qualities and beautifully flawed. You do even get a bit of sexy time. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Terrible,” she managed. “You know how to use this thing?” <br />He pulled away to meet her gaze, and for a minute he was transformed. Still the same features, the lumpy nose and the jutting brow and the hard, dark eyes, but not ugly anymore. Full of character. Full of strength. She looked at his face but she didn’t see it, not the way she had before. The smile spreading across his features was intimate, sexy. The darkness of his eyes concealed so much more than she’d ever imagined. <br />“Oh, aye,” he said. “You gonna let me show you?”</blockquote>
</i><br />I loved Chess as a character too, she’s a very unconventional heroine. I have such a soft spot for those; it just makes me love her more. She’s fucked up, but she knows it. She’s still a good person and she’s strong. Her rough past has made it so she’s never felt safe, she’s a bit paranoid but she’s kind of <i>had to</i> be. <br /><i>
  <blockquote>If her life had taught her anything, it was that you never really knew what people had going on beneath the surface. People were shit. The only difference between them and animals was people felt the need to hide it.</blockquote>
</i><br />I’m really looking forward to learning more about her and seeing her relationships grow. By only gripe is that it’s all told from Chess’s POV, but in third person. I wish this had been in first person, I think I would have connected even more to her. I did love her sarcastic, snarky attitude and the dashes of humor in this though. Can’t wait to dive into the next one! ♥<br /><br /><i>
  <b>Things weren’t so terrible, after all. She was alive. Alive, and just high enough to feel good about it.</b>
</i><br /><br /><i>See this review &amp; others at <a href="http://nobsbookreviews.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">No BS Book Reviews</a>. <br />Also 'like' us on <a href="https://www.facebook.com/NoBsBookReviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a>.</i> ♥<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10517878198868337966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_99815476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/99815476" />
    <a title="Laurie Garrison " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2489609-laurie-garrison"><img alt="Laurie Garrison " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564193945p2/2489609.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/99815476?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie Garrison " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie Garrison " href="/user/show/2489609-laurie-garrison">Laurie Garrison </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2489609-laurie-garrison?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer99815476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10350542777436628067"><br/>For a Urban Fantasy this book was OK for me. The New world is ruled by a church called Church of Real Truth, Stacia explains the world really good and it doesn’t take up the whole storyline. There is lots of hard core action and one somewhat hot scene between Chess and Lex. <br/><br/>Chess has to have her drugs, if not she ends up with the itch. Bump is her supplier. She is in head over heals in debt with him. Bump gives her a ghost hunting job to help pay for what she owes him. From what I read I didn’t </span>
  <span id="freeText10350542777436628067" style="display:none"><br />For a Urban Fantasy this book was OK for me. The New world is ruled by a church called Church of Real Truth, Stacia explains the world really good and it doesn’t take up the whole storyline. There is lots of hard core action and one somewhat hot scene between Chess and Lex. <br /><br />Chess has to have her drugs, if not she ends up with the itch. Bump is her supplier. She is in head over heals in debt with him. Bump gives her a ghost hunting job to help pay for what she owes him. From what I read I didn’t get the whole thing that she was so attraction to Bump’s enforcer there was a little tension there but that’s all I found. But when Lex kidnaps her, so he can get her to do something for him, then you’ll see the attraction kick in. <br /><br />I had a few problems with this book. One is Chess is to much a pill popper for my taste. The other is the dialogue with the drug lords and their people. Here is a few lines “Ain’t you got no people be worried?” or this passage “Bump got the pull. Bump already got that place wide up, see, wide up. But Bump gotta problem. Bump planes-planes carrying them sweet pills you ladybirds like bumps plains crash. Something attacking the planes, dig? Make the go all silent.” Turns they off. This is though the whole book so make sure you can stand this kind of talk between the characters. Even if they talk like this, I found it annoying to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10350542777436628067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_269136568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/269136568" />
    <a title="SubterraneanCatalyst" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5306164-subterraneancatalyst"><img alt="SubterraneanCatalyst" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306967745p2/5306164.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/269136568?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SubterraneanCatalyst" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SubterraneanCatalyst" href="/user/show/5306164-subterraneancatalyst">SubterraneanCatalyst</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8528492-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">UF fans looking for something other than vampires </span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306164-subterraneancatalyst?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306164-subterraneancatalyst?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306164-subterraneancatalyst?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306164-subterraneancatalyst?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5306164-subterraneancatalyst?shelf=post-apocalyptic">post-apocalyptic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269136568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9131101633772234022">I hate to do this but I'm not skilled enough yet to write a review that doesn't have mild spoilers, or even unforgivable spoilers, so forgive me my crutch:<br/><br/> <b>YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED THIS IS SPOILER LAND- THIS SHOULD ONLY BE READ IF YOU'VE ALREADY READ THE BOOK OR YOU JUST DON'T CARE ABOUT KNOWING SOME IMPORTANT PARTS OF THE BOOK UPFRONT, because, I'm just too weak to cleanse my thoughts of them. This probably has more "mild" spoilers.</b><br/><br/>On to business::<br/><br/><p>...Chessie is (in my mind) a luscious tattooed <i>Chur</i></p></span>
  <span id="freeText9131101633772234022" style="display:none">I hate to do this but I'm not skilled enough yet to write a review that doesn't have mild spoilers, or even unforgivable spoilers, so forgive me my crutch:<br><br> <b>YOU HAVE BEEN WARNED THIS IS SPOILER LAND- THIS SHOULD ONLY BE READ IF YOU'VE ALREADY READ THE BOOK OR YOU JUST DON'T CARE ABOUT KNOWING SOME IMPORTANT PARTS OF THE BOOK UPFRONT, because, I'm just too weak to cleanse my thoughts of them. This probably has more "mild" spoilers.</b><br><br>On to business::<br><br><p>...Chessie is (in my mind) a luscious tattooed <i>Churchwitch</i> who is trying to skate through life. I don't think she wants to be noticed. She just wants to blend in and smooth over the edges of her pain with her next fix. I would have posted a bitchin' image of her here somewhere, but lo and behold, if you do google searches of "cute brunette with tattoos" you are in man's land and it's quite pornographic.</p> <br><p> The world of Unholy Ghosts is post apocalyptic and dystopian. Normally this would make me pass on reading a book but even though it's ultra dark and gray I found it worth it and it wasn't mind numbingly dreary. Ghosts with very real power have risen in the world and the churches of old have been abandoned for the Church of Truth. Magic is the only thing that can counter the ghost menace. </p><br><p> I've heard grumbles and rumors of people disliking that Chess takes drugs and perhaps that the ramifications of her drug usage aren't realistic enough given the work she has to pursue, but I disagree completely. I feel Kane gives a satisfying personal history for Chess and her drugs. Does anyone really need a reason to do drugs? Hell, the world she lives in is reason enough. I'd like to point out though that the book indicates (and I wish I had highlighted some quotes but I forgot to) that Chess grew up being beaten, molested and raped in her mother's household. Given this kind of childhood Chess's decisions and behavior toward her relationships is very realistic and consistent. The main tension regarding her drug usage is that she is in a position of some authority being a Churchwitch Debunker and as such has protocol to follow. Failing to adhere to the parameters of her position within the Church of Truth has dire if not deadly consequences. </p><br> <p> Chess embarks on a quest because her friendly neighborhood drug provider, Bump, wants to use her services to banish ghosts at a property that will boost his business. So in comes, Terrible, [Thank you <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/1931718-jan" rel="nofollow noopener">Jan</a> for inspiring my choice of imagery for Terrible, this image is a drawing of Marv from Sin City, and other than hairstyle is how I imagine Terrible] <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368503i/721092.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> the henchman Bump assigns to liaise with Chess during this extra curricular and highly illegal project. Problems arise, naturally, as Chess tries to balance her duties and the illicit project. I'm not going to detail all of the plot but lets just say she has plenty to keep her occupied. </p><br><p> Chess also has to contend with Slobag, another drug dealer and in particular his minion, **Lex: <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380368503i/721093.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">. This book isn't a romance, I would classify it as more of a UF, but there are moments and relationships that will probably be more thoroughly explored in the next books of the series. Most of us that read the UF/PNR genres are jaded about love triangles but I say read this. If you want pure romance don't read this. But I believe her reaction toward Lex is so nicely realistic and her reaction to any possibility of true intimacy is very telling and for me, a fantastic experience in this book. I too am sick of seeing false obstacles that prevent heroines from getting their man when a decent conversation could fix the issue, but here we have a case where it makes complete sense how she interacts with men.</p><br><p> You will find a relatively interesting mystery and investigation, Chess torn between loyalties and her drug habit, mistakes of a very human nature, a spattering of interesting characters (I for one enjoyed Tyson quite a bit and hope to see more this kind of thing in the successive books), some good decently creepy/scary events, and some beautiful moments to be shared with Chess. I am going to read every book of the series, I'm invested and I'm a fan of Kane now!</p><br><br><p>** The beautiful man in that photograph is <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daniel_Henney" rel="nofollow noopener">Daniel Henney</a>, he is half Korean, not Chinese which Lex is supposed to be I think.</p><br> <br><br></span>

<div id="review_98732925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98732925" />
    <a title="Desperado" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado"><img alt="Desperado" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487999118p2/3422821.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98732925?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Desperado" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Desperado" href="/user/show/3422821-desperado">Desperado</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=smack-a-bitch-upside-the-head">smack-a-bitch-upside-the-head</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=paranormal-fiction">paranormal-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=5-and-4-star-ratings">5-and-4-star-ratings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3422821-desperado?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98732925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4881843541982046414"><b>My Thoughts:</b><br/><br/>I received a ARC copy of this novel from GR a few months ago but just recently found the time to read it. Ok, I lied. I was too chickenshit until now to read it after I found out the heroine is a drug addict. You already know the synopsis but I'll give a short recap: Chess is a witch working for the Church helping to banish ghosts. When she racks up a huge debt with her drug dealer, he gives her a job to complete & her debt will be erased & so the story begins.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the world-bui</span>
  <span id="freeText4881843541982046414" style="display:none"><b>My Thoughts:</b><br /><br />I received a ARC copy of this novel from GR a few months ago but just recently found the time to read it. Ok, I lied. I was too chickenshit until now to read it after I found out the heroine is a drug addict. You already know the synopsis but I'll give a short recap: Chess is a witch working for the Church helping to banish ghosts. When she racks up a huge debt with her drug dealer, he gives her a job to complete &amp; her debt will be erased &amp; so the story begins.<br /><br />I enjoyed the world-building in this story of a sort of post-apocalyptic world where God &amp; religion has been proven a myth &amp; the only certainty is power/magic. About 20 something years ago, ghosts came aboveground &amp; started killing people &amp; the Church saved them &amp; banished the ghosts. There are many supporting characters with totally wacked out names &amp; almost all of them are either in gangs or are drug addicts, though a few only do drugs recreationally. There's Bump, Chess's drug dealer whose described as "Frosty the Snowpimp". Terrible, Bump's mega muscle, beating up &amp; killing anyone who gets in Bump's way. Lex, 2nd-in-charge of a rival drug dealer(Slobag) who comes off like a broke-down Jet Li wannabe. Doyle, a rich &amp; spoiled colleague of Chess's at the Church. I didn't like most of the supporting characters but I found Terrible wiggling his way into my heart. First impression is that he's a stupid, ugly enforcer with no mind of his own. But not only is he smarter than anyone thinks, he's also compassionate, caring, loyal &amp; willing to do just about anything to protect those he cares about(some who don't deserve it). I honestly found myself hoping for him to step back onto the scene in some of the passages where he was absent.<br /><br />As for Chess, I'm unsure what to think about her. On one hand, she does have a moral code &amp; there are lines she just won't cross. She cares about other people &amp; everything she does (including almost getting herself killed a few times) isn't just about looking out for number one. On the other hand, I just couldn't get into the whole drug thing. I don't mind druggie heroes/heroines but I personally need there to be a reason for them to turn to narcotics in the first place &amp; for them to at least want to get clean, even if they feel they can't. Chess gives no reason whatsover for why she turned to drugs &amp; even stated that she'd never stop doing it. One chapter she even thought about blowing the cash she'd get from a job on drugs or going to the "pipes"-kind of like an opium den. And don't get me started on how she feels the need to pop a pill right in the beginning or middle of a few action scenes. You'd think she'd want to have a clear head when going after the big baddie,right? I couldn't relate to her as much I would've liked to with a main character.<br /><br />Overall, I enjoyed this novel. I thought the plot was really original &amp; the world Kane has created has me in awe. The action was great, the supernatural crap these characters had to deal with had me creeped out in a good way &amp; there were even a few sexy scenes. I am hoping that Chess will wise the hell up &amp; give up the pill-popping in future novels because I don't think I can root for a heroine who allows herself to be controlled by addiction. I thought this was a great but flawed first-in-series novel by Stacia Kane.<br /><br />BTW, I'd consider this a little more Dark Fantasy then Urban Fantasy although it definitely has a few of the requirements for the latter genre.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4881843541982046414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147843536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3789444051381744264"><b> "Debunking often looks like the most appealing of church positions, but very few possess the skill, intelligence and above all, integrity required."<br/>--Careers In The Church: A Guide For Teens, by Praxis Turpin. </b><br/><br/>My only regret with this book is that I waited so long to read this series. I absolutely <b>LOVE</b> this unique world that even when I'm not reading the book Chess and the Downside World is still on my mind! Fans of the Fever world will fall in live with this world Stacia Kane has created.<br/><br/>Chess</span>
  <span id="freeText3789444051381744264" style="display:none"><b> "Debunking often looks like the most appealing of church positions, but very few possess the skill, intelligence and above all, integrity required."<br />--Careers In The Church: A Guide For Teens, by Praxis Turpin. </b><br /><br />My only regret with this book is that I waited so long to read this series. I absolutely <b>LOVE</b> this unique world that even when I'm not reading the book Chess and the Downside World is still on my mind! Fans of the Fever world will fall in live with this world Stacia Kane has created.<br /><br />Chess is a unique heroine, a Church Witch (a Debunker trained in the art of banishing ghosts) and incredibly likable. Besides her drug addiction, I find her easy to relate to and her inner dialogue is Brilliant!!!!! <br /><br /><br /><b> "Facts are Truth, Sir."<br />The itch was starting to sting. The Grand Elder stayed where he was, starting at the elevator doors. Why didn't he just go already? He had places to be, and she had feet to scratch and uppers to snort.<br /></b><br /><br />Much to my embarrassment in public I found myself laughing aloud while reading this book. Chess is hilarious! <br /><br />Another example of her inner dialogue.<br /><br /><br /><b>If Mrs. Morton would stop verbally jacking off her husband and son this would al be done so much more quickly,but then Chess figured it was just about the only sex the woman got. </b><br /><br /><br />She's also relatable because she's insecure, lonely and easily terrified and doesn't prefer the spotlight or being the "hero".<br /><br /><b> "Stop being such a wimp!"<br /><br />Damn it! She would be down here all night If she didn't grow a pair of fucking ballsand get to that door on the other side. Why was she such a wimp? Why couldn't she--Terrible thought she was brave. She remembered it now, heard his voice in her head as if he stood next to her.<br />"They scared. Not you, though!" Terrible thought she was brave and if he- ( a man whose name was Terrible, a man whose path people scrambled to get out of--thought so it must be true. She could do this, she would do this.<br /></b><br /><br /><br />Also Mrs. Kane introduced a sexy (though not described particularly that way,but he is so very sexy) friend to Chess named Terrible. He's a powerful tatooed bad boy gangster, but with respect to Chess he's quite chivalrous, a<br /> protector, a friend, and I'm pulling for love interest. I found myself anticipating scenes with Terrible in them.<br /><br /><br /><b> "Chess" he mumbled. His lips travelled away, down the side if her throat, eliciting buzzing tingles, that made her entire body vibrate and back upto steal her mouth again. " Chessie. Never thought........so pretty."<br />She could feel the ridge of his erection hot through his jeans. <br />"Terrible." she managed. "You know how to use this thing?"<br />He paused....."Oh, aye," he said. "You gonna let me show you." </b><br /><br />This is only half of the scene, but it's incredibly sensual and sex wasn't even involved. ;)<br /><br />I can't wait to start the next book! I'd you haven't read these yet I suggest you do, I have a new favorite series :)</span>

<div id="review_258253598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258253598" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258253598?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jen by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4335141-miss-vain">MISS VAIN</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258253598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17086792966012210965">As I try to put my thoughts together about this book, I find myself at a little bit of a loss. It's... strange and disturbing at times. But it's also kind of compelling.<br/><br/>The story takes place in an alternate universe where the existence of magic and ghosts are known fact. Society is run by the church. Not any church of God, but one that rejects faith altogether. Its members keep a tight leash on the ghost world. Chess works for the Church as a "debunker." Essentially, she investigates claims of h</span>
  <span id="freeText17086792966012210965" style="display:none">As I try to put my thoughts together about this book, I find myself at a little bit of a loss. It's... strange and disturbing at times. But it's also kind of compelling.<br /><br />The story takes place in an alternate universe where the existence of magic and ghosts are known fact. Society is run by the church. Not any church of God, but one that rejects faith altogether. Its members keep a tight leash on the ghost world. Chess works for the Church as a "debunker." Essentially, she investigates claims of hauntings and gets rid of the ghosts if they are the real deal. She is also a drug addict with no family and no friends.<br /><br />The world Chess lives in is a dark one. Her drug problem is substantial and ever-present. In fact, she owes her dealer some money. But he agrees to cancel her debt if she performs an exorcism for him. And he assigns his enforcer, Terrible, to help her on the job. The story gets more complicated as a scary entity begins stalking Chess, and she must figure out what it is, who sent it, and how to get rid of it.<br /><br />There is alot going on in the story. Too much try to get into here. But it was hard to connect with Chess at first. After all, she is an addict. And she has no real loyalty to speak of --except maybe to the church. She's good at her job, but largely cut off from her own humanity. Terrible, on the other hand, is very easy to sympathize with. He is introduced as he is seen through Chess' eyes, but his true self shines through. He is the strong arm of a drug dealer, but he reads history books; he watches out for the kids on the streets; and he is clearly, completely crazy about Chess.<br /><br />The language in the book takes some getting used to. Most of the characters speak in a street slang that is hard to characterize. And the world is gritty and dark and violent. But there is something intangible that draws me to in, nonetheless. I could say it's because it's unique and fresh. Or that it's because it's unpredictable. Or maybe it's just Terrible. I don't know. I do know that I plan to read the next book, like, right now. --And that Lex has got to go.<br /><br />Very hard to rate. 4 stars? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17086792966012210965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1602622486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer770178108119559974">2.5 stars<br/>This was quite a complex mystery novel and I would recommend it to anyone who is a fan of those types of books. For me this was a kind of love-hate book that had me on the edge of my seat one minute and bored out of my mind the next. There is action and an interesting sense of pace but I'm not going to rate it higher because I took too long to finish it and it didn't compel me enough.<br/><br/>......<br/>This book took place years after Haunted Week which resulted in a lot of spirits of the dead roami</span>
  <span id="freeText770178108119559974" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br />This was quite a complex mystery novel and I would recommend it to anyone who is a fan of those types of books. For me this was a kind of love-hate book that had me on the edge of my seat one minute and bored out of my mind the next. There is action and an interesting sense of pace but I'm not going to rate it higher because I took too long to finish it and it didn't compel me enough.<br /><br />......<br />This book took place years after Haunted Week which resulted in a lot of spirits of the dead roaming and attacking the living by feeding on their lives. It said that the barrier between the world of the living and dead thinned due to astronomical alignments.<br /><br />The characters themselves were well developed and believable and I've got to say I liked Chess quite a lot. Yes she was addicted to drugs but she was always able to keep her wits about her and be sharp minded. She always got her job done despite her addiction and complicated life and I liked that. Terrible felt like quite a complex character that was hiding a lot and I hope in future books there will be a lot more of him and his background. <br /><br />The writing itself was very easy to follow and understand but like I said things for me got boring at times but that usually happens when I'm on a book for too long and don't do a lot of reading. I think overall this was a really good, well written book that would please most fantasy fans and I would recommend it but sadly I lost interest towards the end. Will read on though.</span>

<div id="review_2278938771" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2278938771" />
    <a title="Arunima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27283906-arunima"><img alt="Arunima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598720527p2/27283906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2278938771?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arunima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arunima" href="/user/show/27283906-arunima">Arunima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=my-heart">my-heart</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27283906-arunima?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278938771" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6775188628821755598"><i> Wow, thanks to this book, I have a newly developed phobia of worms. </i> <br/><br/><br/>Unholy Ghosts by Stacia Kane turned out to be more than amazing. I am so glad I decided to read it. <br/><br/>I'll be honest here and admit being extremely picky with my books. I read a lot of reviews ( even though I often get spoilers because of that ), check the average rating before choosing it.<br/>Usually when the rating's below 4, I get really sceptical about the book and often don't keep very high expectations. I know it's bad and wro</span>
  <span id="freeText6775188628821755598" style="display:none"><i> Wow, thanks to this book, I have a newly developed phobia of worms. </i> <br><br><br>Unholy Ghosts by Stacia Kane turned out to be more than amazing. I am so glad I decided to read it. <br><br>I'll be honest here and admit being extremely picky with my books. I read a lot of reviews ( even though I often get spoilers because of that ), check the average rating before choosing it.<br>Usually when the rating's below 4, I get really sceptical about the book and often don't keep very high expectations. I know it's bad and wrong  but I can't help  it. <br>Doesn't mean i dont read books with less ratings. I try all sorts of books because I like it when I am not expecting much from a book but it turns out be really good. Like five stars good. <br><br><br>The overall rating of this book is apparently "3.63" which isn't that great and after reading a lot of other reviews I think I understand it. This book is quite a complex one. <br><br><br>It's very different from the other Urban Fantasies that I have read. It's graphic, darker and not all that pretty. <br>Too much drugs. Too many slangs.<br>And there is some really freaky shit in here which left me with actual goosebumps and racing hearts. <br><br><br>I have noticed a lot of people not liking Chess here as a protagonist. Which is understandable. She is not your usual badass MC. She is badass alright but she isn't all that strong all the time. She needs her drugs to go on with each day. <br>Now I admit myself, I hate drugs and smoking with a passion. I don't judge other people who engage in it at all. It's just a personal opinion. But the thing is that when I am reading a book, I try to connect with the protagonist. Relate with her. And yes, I was put off with Chess' addiction at the beginning. She isn't just a regular drug abuser. She is a full blown junkie who has to take multiple pills and smokes a day. Without remorse or regret.<br><br><br>At one point I was so disturbed by the whole thing that I finally decided to take a beat. I closed the book and did some thinking. It was important for me to understand Chess as a character. Why is she like this. It wasn't fair to dislike a character because of a problem she has. A lot of people have this problem and it's very important to <i> understand </i> them. <br><br><br>Chess has gone through a lot as a child. When she wasn't even ten yet, she had been subjected to all sorts of physical and sexual assualts. She had a hard time growing up. I also learnt the reason for her addiction which isn't mentioned in this book. It isn't really a spoiler but it makes a lot more sense. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Her foster parents gave her regular doses of drugs to keep her under control.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>Chess has a lot of problems but she is a self dependent and strong minded woman. Drugs is her only weakness. I don't love her. No, not yet. But I really do admire her. <br><br><br>And coming to my favourite part of the whole book : Terrible. <br>I don't have words to explain what I feel for him. How much I am in love with him.<br><br>Terrible is ugly.  <br><br><i> Urban Fantasy and an ugly male love interest!? How in the world did that happen?Hell must have frozen over. </i> I know right. That's what made me love this book so much more. How different it was from other urban fantasy stereotypes. <br><br><b> <i> <br><br>“Nothing here, Chess, nothing here.” She didn’t know how many times he said it before it finally sank in, before the queasy vibrating stopped in her legs and she could raise her head and look at him.<br> <br>“Thought you was good with the spook stuff,” he said. “You look like some dead.”<br> <br>“And you look like Elvis vomited you up,” she managed. “So?”<br> <br>Hinges creaked in her ears again as he laughed. “So we both looking bad, guesses. But I do always, and you do never. You right now?” </i> </b><br><br><br><br>Terrible is such a precious character, 6'4, with large jutting eyebrows, scarred face, large crooked nose but at the same time he is the most beautiful character in there. Also he is hot as hell and kissed like a motherfu**** wet dream. He is scary alright, doesn't talk much and has speech issues but he is such a sweetheart. It also shows how much he cares for Chess more than just a friend even though he hasn't said anything as of yet. <br><br><br>We also have another male love interest. Now I usually avoid love triangles like plague because I just hate it when a girl is confused between her two lovers moving back and forth and especially when she chooses the wrong one. But here, I don't have much problem with it. Lex, the other guy is super scorching hot Asian drug dealer. There is a lot of attraction between them but I don't see any romance. I really like Lex but I have a strong feeling that Terrible and Chess will be endgame, since it makes much more sense. Lex and Chess are attracted to each other but it doesn't feel anything. It happened too early. But with Terrible, you get to see a lot of relationship development. Nothing much has happened between them but that's what later books are for. <br><br><br>The rest of the book otherwise is incredible. It took me a lot of time though at the beginning to grasp the world building. But the writing is amazing. Especially the messed up English that almost everyone except Chess had. As I said before as well, there is some really freaky stuff in here. It's dark and raw.<br><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1525603853ra/25490076.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Happy Reading :)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6775188628821755598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_69657207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69657207" />
    <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer"><img alt="Carolyn  Storer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457826767p2/2449271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69657207?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn  Storer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn  Storer" href="/user/show/2449271-carolyn-storer">Carolyn  Storer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007352814" href="/book/show/8086283-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2449271-carolyn-storer?shelf=book-list-2010">book-list-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69657207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16055506470024788710"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I'm so excited about this book - I LOVED it! I haven't read an Urban Fantasy this good in quite a while. I've read the first in Kane's 'Megan Chase' series, but she's come on leaps and bounds since then, Unholy Ghosts is just so much better in every respect.<br/><br/>The writing is perfectly paced, I didn't get bored once and everything slots together at the right time. The plot is just brilliant and had me engrossed until the very last page - I didn't want to put this book down!<br/><br/>The characters ar</span>
  <span id="freeText16055506470024788710" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I'm so excited about this book - I LOVED it! I haven't read an Urban Fantasy this good in quite a while. I've read the first in Kane's 'Megan Chase' series, but she's come on leaps and bounds since then, Unholy Ghosts is just so much better in every respect.<br /><br />The writing is perfectly paced, I didn't get bored once and everything slots together at the right time. The plot is just brilliant and had me engrossed until the very last page - I didn't want to put this book down!<br /><br />The characters are fantastic, very well rounded and completely believable. Chess is everything I want in my urban fantasy heroine: kick-arse but flawed, vulnerable and complex. I have a feeling she's going to be one of my favourites within this genre (with Anita Blake at no. 1 at the moment).<br /><br />Chess is a witch and a ghost hunter, with a serious drug problem. She's constantly popping pills to get her through the day. In fact she has different pills for different situations and choses accordingly. Obviously I don't condone the use of drugs but sometimes life is too difficult for some people to handle and Chess is one of them - using drugs to get through life, and that's why I have so much sympathy for her. I loved the rawness of Chess, she's real and vulnerable with a past that gives me full understanding of why she pops so many pills - to forget. A past full of physical and mental abuse, shipped from one foster home to another. I liked her from the get-go. Kane has created one hell of a heroine.<br /><br />So now I've talked a little about Chess, let's get on to the guys. I have not met a character like Terrible in any other urban fantasy book. He's not the typical dreamy looking, squared jawed hunk, but a rugged, built like a brick house, rough and ready dude with a crooked nose that's been broken too many times to count. Doesn't sound very attractive does he. But the way Kane reveals his personality through his actions and dialogue is just superb, and well, I just fell totally in love with him myself! He's as complex as Chess, with a dark past to match. In fact they have a lot in common. I really enjoyed their developing relationship and I can't wait to see where it's going in subsequent novels.<br /><br />There's also another guy on the scene, Lex, a leader of a rival gang. He is described as a gorgeous male and Chess can't but not like the look of him. And I don't blame her, but for all his charm there is something untrustworthy about him and I have my doubts. But with Terrible, I feel he has Chess' back and her best interests at heart. He shows his loyalty many times throughout Unholy Ghosts and it has cemented his fate in becoming one of my favourite hero's in urban fantasy.<br /><br />Terrible is Bump's top enforcer and doesn't flinch at the prospect of killing someone in cold blood. They are thrown together at the request of Bump, who Chess owes several thousands pounds, to find out what is haunting his airport and whatever it is, he wants Chess to fix it. The world building is spot on. I could smell and see everything described. The world is quite a sombre place and Chess lives where drugs are rife and life is hard. Her only real home is the Church. But the Church of Real Truth isn't like any religion we know today, but almost a dictator that holds the fear of ghosts over the heads of the living. If they do not follow them and do as they wish then they will release all ghosts upon them and they will die. I'm intrigued to find out if the Church of Real Truth are the good guys or the bad, but at the moment I don't trust them.<br /><br />All supporting characters are also vivid and not one of them felt unrealistic or surplus to the plot, from the young boy looking for help to the terrifying Dreamthief. Unholy Ghosts is a gritty, fairly dark urban fantasy, but this is fine with me as it's my favourite kind!<br /><br />Verdict:<br /><br />I think I have squealed enough about this book, so let's just finish by saying that I cannot wait to read the rest of the series - I've heard it gets even better! Unholy Ghosts is a brilliant addition to the Urban Fantasy genre and I can't recommend it enough!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16055506470024788710" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_274159180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274159180" />
    <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence"><img alt="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559561558p2/6186603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274159180?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeann (Happy Indulgence) " href="/user/show/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence">Jeann (Happy Indulgence) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007352814" href="/book/show/8086283-unholy-ghosts">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=dark-and-gritty">dark-and-gritty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6186603-jeann-happy-indulgence?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274159180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1552397243218461306">While reading Unholy Ghosts, what struck me was how strange and unusual it was in some parts of it's storytelling. <br/><br/>Chess is a witch who hunts ghosts for a living, but she is also addicted to drugs and uses them to deal with her life. In order to use magic, she is an employee of the Church of Real Truth, yet she also hangs out in all the wrong places. This juxta-positioning was a little strange, especially when she snorts drugs, listens to sermons, and hangs around rough-talking males. She certai</span>
  <span id="freeText1552397243218461306" style="display:none">While reading Unholy Ghosts, what struck me was how strange and unusual it was in some parts of it's storytelling. <br /><br />Chess is a witch who hunts ghosts for a living, but she is also addicted to drugs and uses them to deal with her life. In order to use magic, she is an employee of the Church of Real Truth, yet she also hangs out in all the wrong places. This juxta-positioning was a little strange, especially when she snorts drugs, listens to sermons, and hangs around rough-talking males. She certainly is an intriguing character, definitely not predictable or run-of-the-mill in any sense. I'm still unsure whether she's a likable one or not, but I guess I'll just have to wait and see as the series unfolds. <br /><br />The book features an interesting and unique setting. It's set in a dystopian world based around ghosts, where a Church has been established to deal with the ghost problem. As the first in the series definitely had a lot of world-building to it. Despite this, a perfect sense of pace between mystery, character development, and world building sucked me into the story. <br /><br />Chess's drug using however, was a bit hard to swallow (no pun intended). She's describe as an addict and that she definitely is and we hear about her need throughout the book.<br /><br />The men in the book were kind of strange. I don't really buy Chess being attracted to either of them, and they are both are written a bit too similar in my opinion. They're both from opposing gangs, and both use rougher, street speech to talk, and both apparently perfect gentlemen. I kind of find this difficult to believe, but I suppose they are meant to be love interests.<br /><br />I'm glad I've picked up this series as I've heard it gets really good later on and will be definitely continuing to read it.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.happyindulgencebooks.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Check out Happy Indulgence for more reviews!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1552397243218461306" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer421999919" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6054434190243151216">I am SO grateful to have found this series. <br/>Completely original and addictive storytelling. Deeply flawed characters that I still managed to care about.<br/><br/>This book also features several characters who speak with what can only be described as a kind of intensely grammatically incorrect dialect that would normally be a deal breaker for me when it comes to reading and enjoying a book. I'm not sure if it was just the fact that the dialect made sense in the scope of the story, or if I have gotten more </span>
  <span id="freeText6054434190243151216" style="display:none">I am SO grateful to have found this series. <br />Completely original and addictive storytelling. Deeply flawed characters that I still managed to care about.<br /><br />This book also features several characters who speak with what can only be described as a kind of intensely grammatically incorrect dialect that would normally be a deal breaker for me when it comes to reading and enjoying a book. I'm not sure if it was just the fact that the dialect made sense in the scope of the story, or if I have gotten more easy-going in my old age (i'm betting on the first option) but it didn't bother me at all here. In fact, i actually thought the way that my favorite character Trouble spoke was...kind of cool. I know, it's weird, right?! <br /><br />The only thing keeping me from giving this 5 stars was the fact that I found the story slightly confusing towards the end. But, otherwise...this book totally rocked!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S81K58trfGwxTz196ZkjV/tMPakfJdtkS69F5IKZ7zQrxH6JuVwUzrMyiD3lVgYKzBXRehvYHs7/cK8Ij6XkTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Ef7YtyDQwcgT76dWatqMG5+KQmh0bH80zkgHksHmfSZx9+zZUuepapGSEhZmFalGqNOuu3CRup56l+1+zNp2Xg==')})
  }
